WELL EVALUATION
View of Cyclone 5 with flare while drilling at the Mooka 6-20-29TFH in Mountrail County, North Dakota
on August 10, 2014 (All photos by Gerald Jett, Sunburst Consulting Inc.).
Introduction
The Slawson Exploration Company, Inc. Mooka 6-29-20TFH [SW SW Section 29,
T152N, R92W] is located approximately one mile south of New Town in Mountrail
County, North Dakota. The location lies within the Big Bend Field of the Williston Basin,
where Slawson Exploration Company, Inc. is producing from the Three Forks and using
hydraulic fracturing techniques to create new fractures and enhance natural fractures to
draw from the pool.
The Mooka 6-29-20TFH was planned as a two section lateral extending 9,629' at a heading
of 4.63° from the SW quarter of the SW quadrant of Section 29, T152N, R92W to the NE
quarter of the NW quadrant of Section 20, T152N, R92W.
OFFSET WELLS
The primary offset well used to develop a prognosis of formation tops was the Slawson
Exploration Company, Inc. MacCougar 4-30-19TFH, which is 0.58 miles west of the
subject well. The Slawson Exploration Company, Inc., Mooka 5-29-20TFH (80' west) and
the Mooka 3-29-20TFH, (0.50 miles east) were also used as offset wells. Each of these
wells played an intricate part in landing of the build section for lateral operations.
ENGINEERING
The surface hole was spud July 3, 2014 and drilled to a depth of 1,920' MD with one 13
½" Atlas PDC bit in 10.5 hours. Surface casing was set to 1,920' MD and consisted of 46
joints of 9 " 36# J-55. The vertical hole was drilled with two 8 ¾" Ulterra U616M PDC
bits to a KOP depth of 9,739' MD.
At kick-off point, the curve build began at 9,739' MD. Weatherford Directional Drilling
Company provided directional drilling and MWD personnel, tools and equipment. MWD
surveys from the vertical hole provided survey tie-in data for curve and lateral surveys. An
Ulterra U516M PDC bit ahead of a fixed 2.58° fixed motor drilled 893' of curve in 24.5
hours with a landing 27' below the top of the Three Forks. The curve was landed at a
10,632' MD at approximately 10,151' TVD with a projected inclination of 89.77°. An
intermediate casing string consisting of 266 joints of 7" 32# HCP-110 was then set to
10,624' MD and cemented.
The lateral was drilled with one 6" Hughes T406X PDC bit ahead of a 1.5 Bico motor to
17,327' MD in 111.5 hours before being pulled for an inability to slide. This assembly was
replaced by a 6" Smith MDSI613 PDC bit head of another 1.5 Bico motor drilling 2,815'
in 39.5 hours. Total depth of 20,142' MD was reached at 19:45 CDT on August 14, 2014.
The bottom hole location is 261.53' FNL and 1,944.12' FWL NE NW Section 20, T152N,
R92W. Projected to TD, the wellbore is 9,854.67' north and 764.12' east of the surface
location with a closure direction of 4.43°, resulting in a closure distance of 9,884.25'.
Freshwater based drilling fluid was used while drilling the surface hole, oil-based invert
drilling fluid (10.10 to 11.30 lb/gal) was utilized for the vertical and curve, while saltwater
drilling fluid (9.60 to 10.10 lb/gal) was used for the lateral portion.
GEOLOGY
Methods
Geologic supervision was provided by a Sunburst Consulting, Inc. geology team, which
logged drill cuttings, monitored mud gas and provided on-site geo-steering consultation.
Geologic evaluation began at 7,900' MD and continued until the well reached a total depth
of 20,142' MD. Rig crew members caught 30' lagged samples under direction of the well-
site geologists. Cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope, while cut
fluorescence was observed under UV light with Trichloroethylene, (Carbo-sol), cutting
agent. Lithologic descriptions are provided as an appendix to this report. A digital gas
detector, (MLogger total gas with chromatograph), was interfaced with a Pason electronic
data recorder system. Pason provided depth, drill rates and pump information to the gas
detection computer and received total gas information for viewing around location. Total
gas was recorded as units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air) and chromatography
of C1­C4 components were calculated in parts-per-million.
Lithology and hydrocarbon shows
The siltstone and sandstone of the Big Snowy Group's Kibbey Formation was present when
geologic evaluation began. The Kibbey "Lime" was not part of the geologic evaluation.
The Charles Salt was drilled at 7,963' MD, 7,963' TVD (-6,051'). This interval was
identified by its translucent to transparent, trace milky, hard, euhedral to sub-hedral,
crystalline salt with intervals of white to off white, microcrystalline, soft to friable, earthy
limestone, which was argillaceous in part, and a white to off white, soft, massive,
amorphous anhydrite (Figure 1).
Figure 1. Charles Salt [45x wet].
The Mission Canyon Formation was drilled at 8,668' MD, 8,667' TVD (-6,755') and
consisted of an off white, cream, trace light gray, microcrystalline, soft to friable limestone
that has an earthy texture and is argillaceous in part (Figure 2).
Figure 2. Mission Canyon limestone [45x wet].
The Lodgepole Formation was drilled at 9,295' MD, 9,294' TVD (-7,382') and primarily
consisted of argillaceous limestone described as a mudstone that is light to medium brown,
cream to tan, trace light gray, crystalline and soft to friable with an earthy texture and trace
disseminated pyrite with trace amounts of an off white to cream, light gray,
microcrystalline, earthy limestone that is argillaceous in part and contained no visible
porosity (Figure 3).
Figure 3. Lodgepole [45x wet].
The False Bakken was drilled at 10,162' MD, 10,103' TVD (-8,191') and was identified
by a dark gray, dark gray brown, soft to friable, blocky, carbonaceous shale with an earthy
texture and common disseminated pyrite (Figure 4).
Figure 4. False Bakken and Scallion [45x wet].
The Upper Bakken Shale was drilled at 10,181' MD, 10,119' TVD (-8,207') and
consisted of a dark gray, dark gray brown, soft to friable, blocky, earthy, petroliferous,
carbonaceous shale which contained common disseminated pyrite and no visible porosity
(Figure 5).
Figure 5. Upper Bakken Shale [45x wet].
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 10,215' MD, 10,134' TVD (-8,222'). This Bakken
member consisted of a light gray, light gray brown, trace medium gray, friable to firm,
moderately sorted, calcite and dolomitic cemented silty sandstone that contained trace
disseminated pyrite and exhibited trace intergranular porosity and trace spotty light brown
oil stain (Figure 6).
Figure 6. Middle Bakken. [45x wet].
The Lower Bakken Shale was penetrated at 10,305' MD, 10,184' TVD (-8,272') and
consisted of a dark gray, dark gray brown, soft to friable, blocky, earthy, petroliferous, and
carbonaceous shale, which contained common disseminated pyrite and no visible porosity
(Figure 7).
Figure 7. Lower Bakken Shale. [45x wet].
The Three Forks Formation was penetrated at 10,415' MD, 10,224' TVD (-8,312'). This
formation consisted of a sandstone described as tan to light brown, light gray, trace cream,
very fine grained, friable, subangular to subrounded, poorly to moderately sorted,
moderately cemented with calcite to dolomite cemented, with trace disseminated pyrite and
trace light brown spotty oil stain and is interbedded with a pale green, soft to firm,
subblocky to blocky, earthy shale with trace disseminated pyrite (Figure 8).
Figure 8. Three Forks. [45x wet].
Gas shows (C1-C4) in the target zone were moderate throughout the lateral, with
background gases slowly climbing throughout, dependent upon position within formation.
Background gases were consistently around 200 to 400 units the early portions of the lateral
and increases to 1,000 to 2,000 units in the middle portion of the lateral, until running
through the gas buster began, which dropped background gas to 300 to 500 units and
remained consistent to TD (Figure 9). These gas levels were recorded against 9.60 to 10.10
lb/gal mud. Trace light brown spotty oil staining and cut fluorescence were observed in
samples throughout the lateral.
Figure 9. MController screen image of the Three Forks target interval indicating background gas with
corresponding chromatograph readings.
Geo-steering
The target zone was defined by the Slawson Exploration Company, Inc project geologist
as a 9' thick interval beginning approximately 21' below the top of the Three Forks
Formation in an area of increased porosity. A TVD type log, created by Weatherford
MWD, (Figure 10), was utilized by Sunburst Consulting geologists to correlate the gamma
ray signature of formation markers during the steering of the lateral in order to determine
stratigraphic position and local apparent dip. In addition, samples, drilling parameters, type
logs and gas shows were interpreted to aid in the understanding of the wellbore's
stratigraphic position.
Figure 10. Mooka 5-29-20TFH target (Gerald Jett,
Sunburst Consulting geologist).
The drilling plan was to land 20' below the top of the Three Forks within the area of higher
porosity. From Three Forks entry to TD a gross apparent dip of 0.18° up was interpreted
(Figure 11). On two occasions the wellbore exited the top of zone and exited the base of
zone on two separate occasions. At 10,562' MD the wellbore exited the base of the target
and remained out of zone until 111,405' MD. At 11,840' MD the wellbore exited the top
of zone and remained out until 12,788' MD. The wellbore again exited the top of zone at
15,565' MD before re-entering at 16,509' MD. The wellbore exited the base of the target
interval at 18,064' MD, re-entered at 19,721' MD, then remained in the target interval until
reaching total depth at 20,142' MD.
Figure 11. Cross sectional interpretation of dip illustrating gas, MWD gamma ray and ROP.
SUMMARY
1)
Mooka 6-29-20TFH was drilled to 20,142' MD with a lateral exposure of 9,510'.
2)
The well was spud on July 3, 2014 for surface, vertical and curve operations. The
well was drilled from surface to curve landing utilizing four bits in 129 drilling
hours. The well was re-entered on August 5, 2014 for lateral operation. The total
depth was reached after 22 drilling days on August 14, 2014.
3)
Diesel-based drilling fluid (10.10 to 11.30 lb/gal) was utilized from surface casing
to a curve landing of 10,632' MD. Saltwater based drilling fluid (9.60 to 10.10
lb/gal) was successfully utilized throughout lateral portion of the well.
4)
The wellbore exited the base of the Three Forks target interval on two separate
occasions and exited the top of the target interval on two separate occasions. The
wellbore remained within the target zone for approximately 66% of the lateral.
Overall apparent dip of the target zone was estimated at 0.18° up.
5)
Background gases (C1-C4) were consistently around 200 to 400 units the early
portions of the lateral and increases to 1000 to 2000 units in the latter parts, until
running through the gas buster began, which dropped background gas to 300 to 500
units and remained consistent to TD
6)
The Mooka 6-29-20TFH is currently awaiting completion and enhanced
stimulation efforts to determine its ultimate production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Gerald Jett
Lead Well-site Geologist and
Geo-steering Consultant
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
August 15, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught lagged samples, under the supervision of Sunburst geologists, in 30' intervals from 7,900' to
20,142' MD (TD). Gamma ray marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference.
Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Drilling fluid was diesel-based invert from
surface casing though an intermediate casing point of 10,632'MD and saltwater from intermediate casing to a total
depth of 20,142' MD.
Drilling in Kibbey
7900-7930 SILTSTONE reddish brown, trace light brown, soft, blocky to subblocky, earthy texture, trace
disseminated pyrite, no visible porosity
7930-7962 SILTSTONE reddish brown, trace light brown, soft, blocky to subblocky, earthy texture, trace
disseminated pyrite, no visible porosity

RE:
HORIZONTAL WELL
MOOKA 6-29-20TFH
SWSW Section 29-152N-92W
Mountrail County
Well File # 28620
Dear Khem:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 22418, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 20 & 29, T152N, R92W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted.
Conductor may only be set for the permitted wells on the pad.
SLAWSON
EXPLORATION must contact NDIC Field Inspector Robert Garbe at 701-720-3262 prior to location
construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 9915' north .
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Khem Suthiwan
June 13, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Nathaniel Erbele
Petroleum Resource Specialist

RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.

Slawson Pre-Frac Safety and Testing Procedure
7" casing testing procedure
1) Logging
a. Run bond log to top of L/H/P and ensure adequate cement coverage (at least 500' above top of zone to
be fractured)
b. Run casing inspection log in 7" casing to top of L/H/P or 100' beneath cement top
i. De-rate casing for any significant wear based on remaining wall thickness.
ii. Set maximum treating pressure at no more than 85% of the normal or de-rated pressure rating -
whichever applies.
2) Casing testing
a. RU wireline and set a test plug in the top of the Liner/Hanger/Packer.
b. Pressure test the 7" casing and wellhead as follows:
i. In new areas where treating pressures are unknown, test to 7500# for 30 minutes with less than
a 5% loss
ii. In areas with established operations, test to 500# above fracturing pressures seen in that area for
30 minutes with less than a 5% loss
iii. In the case of worn casing, if 85% of the de-rated pressure rating results in a maximum
allowable treating pressure that is less than 500# greater than the expected treating pressure ­
run a tie-back string
3) Pressure relief valve ­ an adequately sized pressure relief valve must be installed on the treating lines from
the pump to the wellhead and set to limit the line pressure to no more than the casing test pressure less 100#.
4) Surface casing valve ­ the surface casing valve must be left open and a diversion line run to a pit or
containment vessel; in order to enable relief of any pressure encountered in the surface casing/intermediate
casing annulus during fracture operations.
Fracturing Check List
1) Spot tanks
2) Install water manifold
3) Fill tanks
4) Add biocide and scale inhibitor and heat/mix water
5) Install 10,000# manually operated frac valve on tubing head
6) Install 10,000# remotely-activated, hydraulically-actuated valve
7) Install 10,000# frac tree
8) Install ball-catcher
9) RU flowback crew as much as possible
10) Stake lines down and secure all flowback equipment
11) Treat well
12) Initiate flowback and wait for sand to cleanup and oil cut to reach 15% before turning to the battery
13) After flowback is complete, shut well in and rig down the flowback crew
14) RD ball catcher and send back to Stinger
15) RD frac tree and send back to Frontier
16) RD hydraulically actuated valve and send back to Frontier
17) Leave manually operated master valve for well control
18) Turn well over to production
19) When it's time to run tubing, send manually operated master valve back to Frontier
The SHL is 440' FSL & 1,180' FWL (SWSW), Section 29, T152N, R92W, Mountrail
County, ND. The state setback from the section lines are 500' FEL & FWL, 200' FSL &
FNL.
7" Casing: 8-3/4" hole: KOP at 9,728'. Build curve at 12°/100' to 90° inclination at
10,478' MD (10,205' TVD) at an azimuth of 41.63°, and set 7" casing (797' FSL &
1497' FWL, SESW, Section 29, T152N, R92W).
Lateral: After drilling out of the 7" casing shoe, decrease azimuth to 0° at 3°/100'. Drill
a 6" horizontal well holding an azimuth of 0° to TD at a depth of 20,106' MD (10,205'
TVD), 250' FNL & 1980' FWL (NENW) Section 20, T152N , R92W. Expect an
inclination of 90.00°. Total 6" lateral is 9,629'.
